Introduction

The scenario described in this document, is one where an enduser is user an external service, for managing and printing documents. This in turns delegates the management of printing and printjobs to a seperate service, Printix. From a brids eye view the process is:

  1. The Service authenticates with the printix Api as a service principal

  2. When Performing actions on behalf of an individual user (Which is basically all actions), the Service must use the credentials provided in Step 1 to get a special token which identifies that user.

  3. The token aquired in step 2 is used to create Printjobs on behalf of the user.

Creating on or more printjobs consists of multiple steps.

  1. Selecting a printer

  2. Fetching the user specific job URL

  3. Creating the job by posting metadata to the user specific job URL

  4. Uploading the job data (usually PDF) to a URL given in the response. This is a signed and secure URL in a cloud datastore such as Azure blob storage, Google Cloud store or Amazon S3.

  5. Informing the Printix Api that the upload is complete.

Printjobs belong to a given user on a specific tenant, as such, when creating printjobs, we begin traversing the api from the list of tenants accessible to the current user.

Authentication

The service interacting with Printix must first aquire a set of service tokens. This is done using the Client Credentials flow of oauth 2

The service is provided, out of band, with a credential set consisting of a clientid and a client secret. These are posted to the printix token endpoint.

$ curl 'https://auth.printix.net/oauth/token'  -X POST \
    -H 'Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded'\
    -d 'grant_type=client_credentials&client_id={clientId}&client_secret={clientSecret}

In case of success the response will be

Content-Type: application/json;charset=UTF-8

{
  "access_token": "5a8c4ec4-ff70-4f4c-b088-29a8cae38062",
  "refresh_token": "e6f05338-9d27-466b-afa8-0ce72945da7d",
  "expires_in": 599
}

When the service has to perform actions on behalf of a user, it will use the token endpoint to exchange the refresh token to a user scoped token.

$ curl 'https://auth.printix.net/oauth/token'  -X POST \
    -H 'Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded'\
    -d 'grant_type=refresh_token&client_id={clientId}&client_secret={clientSecret}&scope=user.{userId}&refresh_token={refreshToken}

Note the scope is specified as the literal string user. followed by the users id. so a correct scope could be

'user.b425170d-2bed-422d-94b1-b66796e44069'

If the credentials are correct the server will respond

Content-Type: application/json;charset=UTF-8

{
  "access_token": "5a8c4ec4-ff70-4f4c-b088-29a8cae38062",
  "expires_in": 599
}

Note the lack of refresh token in the response.

Get tenants

Request structure

$ curl 'https://api.devenv.printix.net/v1/users/me' -i -X GET \
    -H 'Accept: application/json' \
    -H 'Authorization: Bearer 1767dcaf-85d2-4366-97fe-1aac4d7d4c0b'

Response structure

Relation Description

px:currentuser

URL of a tenant specific version of the user performing the call(or the user the call is being performed on behalf of)

px:printers

URL of the printers available to the current user (or the user the call is being performed on behalf of)

Links

Relation Description

self

selflink

Create Printjob

Creating the job, is a simple form post

Request structure

$ curl 'https://api.devenv.printix.net/v1/tenants/c57bc29a-2d99-43d2-8b6a-db5b0c65ac26/users/3c15bbf8-5680-440d-86e4-cc791075627d/printjobs' -i -X POST \
    -H 'Accept: application/json' \
    -H 'Authorization: Bearer 1767dcaf-85d2-4366-97fe-1aac4d7d4c0b' \
    -H 'Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded; charset=ISO-8859-1' \
    -d 'jobName=TestJob&color=false&printer=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.devenv.printix.net%2Fv1%2Ftenants%2Fc57bc29a-2d99-43d2-8b6a-db5b0c65ac26%2Fprinters%2F3751e90c-ce42-4d52-84b6-ef9e9d7e77ea&queue=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.devenv.printix.net%2Fv1%2Ftenants%2Fc57bc29a-2d99-43d2-8b6a-db5b0c65ac26%2Fprinters%2F3751e90c-ce42-4d52-84b6-ef9e9d7e77ea%2Fqueues%2Fff356ed7-c535-4152-a049-7f0cb470c6fa&page_size=ISOA4'

Links

Relation Description

self

selflink

px:upload

Signed Cloud storage link, where the job data can be uploaded

px:uploadCompleted

URL to notify the Printix Api on, when the job data has been uploaded

Upload Job data

The response from the job creation contains a signed upload link, and an uploadHeaders property. The shape and content of these properties depends on the tenant configuration, but will point to some kind of cloud storage(Azure Blob storage, Google Cloud Storage or AWS S3) this link + upload headers contains all required authentication information, so even in the case of an intermidiary server, interacting with the printix api on behalf of a specific user, the upload can be done directly from the enduser client. The data is uploaded by PUTting to the url in the link, with the headers from uploadHeaders set.

Finalize upload

Once the job data is uploaded, the client informs the Printix Api that the job is ready.

Request structure

$ curl 'https://api.devenv.printix.net/v1/tenants/c57bc29a-2d99-43d2-8b6a-db5b0c65ac26/printjobs/dedd3978-c627-4524-b3e0-a6b4a3ed3dc9/uploadCompleted?jobName=TestJob&color=false&printer=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.devenv.printix.net%2Fv1%2Ftenants%2Fc57bc29a-2d99-43d2-8b6a-db5b0c65ac26%2Fprinters%2F3751e90c-ce42-4d52-84b6-ef9e9d7e77ea&queue=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.devenv.printix.net%2Fv1%2Ftenants%2Fc57bc29a-2d99-43d2-8b6a-db5b0c65ac26%2Fprinters%2F3751e90c-ce42-4d52-84b6-ef9e9d7e77ea%2Fqueues%2Fff356ed7-c535-4152-a049-7f0cb470c6fa&page_size=ISOA4' -i -X GET \
    -H 'Authorization: Bearer 1767dcaf-85d2-4366-97fe-1aac4d7d4c0b' \
    -H 'Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded; charset=ISO-8859-1'
